## Boldur's orebiter
*5 posts · started by Ropewarrior on 2025-01-05* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3434966)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1140135` · 2025-01-05

Thematically, Orebiter is such a fun card, but as we play with it, it seems pretty OP. The equipment card allows Boldur to attach adjacent mountain areas and each hit generates a gold. I think maybe we're using it incorrectly as it's generating a massive amount of gold and allow upgrades very easily.

Since it's an equipment card, I know we can only use it once per round. Since it triggers an attack (not an action, just a roll for damage), am I right in that any weapon modifiers CAN be used in that attack but would then NOT be available for an Attack Action later in that same turn? 

For example, Boldur's upgraded character card allows him to roll 5 dice in an attack. He also has Eitri's Pick, which is a Main Weapon and grants +2 dice. If this character wanted to use Orebiter, could he roll 7 dice but then on an Attack Action that turn, only roll 5, since he "used" Eitri's pick to attack a mountain?

Unrelated, but I backed this on KS with my 11-year old son in mind. He isn't a huge gamer but loves Castle Panic and LOVES mythology. This came right before Christmas and he didn't seem super interested at first, but my 9-year old and I talked him into playing and he absolutely loves this game and begs us to play it. So thank you for a great game that allows us to have quality time together!

---
**#2** · user `36112` · 2025-01-05 *(edited)*

I believe the card simply provides you the additional option to attack mountains with your Attack Action.  Instead of being able to attack only Monsters with your Attack Action, you can now attack Monsters and Mountains.  It is a passive ability that isn't "used", it's a modifier for your normal Attack Action.

 (and actually, if you did get multiple Attack Actions in one turn, which you can with one of Boldur's abilities, the passive ability could trigger multiple times in one turn)

[q="Ropewarrior"]Since it triggers an attack (not an action, just a roll for damage), am I right in that any weapon modifiers CAN be used in that attack but would then NOT be available for an Attack Action later in that same turn?[/q]

Also, I believe you might have something slightly wrong -- Weapon [+ Axe] modifiers modify only Attack Actions -- they are never available to be applied to "roll" effects.
But in the Orebiter case, you would be able to use those modifiers, since you are rolling for an attack with your Attack Action.

[q="Ropewarrior"]he absolutely loves this game and begs us to play it. So thank you for a great game that allows us to have quality time together![/q]
It really is great!!

---
**#3** · user `1140135` · 2025-01-05

Thanks for the quick reply! This makes sense!

---
**#4** · user `4122623` · 2025-01-05

Like Anthony said, you are attacking a mountain, not monsters AND using your attack action on your player board to do it. So you are rolling to hit the gold vein and all damage done is gained as gold, but you can't attack monsters with your attack action on the same turn. You still have swift strike available though.

You do have to pay 2 gold to get the orebiter, but as the card says [i]The potential gain is endless[/i]

---
**#5** · user `1140135` · 2025-01-05

I think what threw us off was it says "you may attack adjacent mountain areas" but didn't mention an Attack Action, like some of the other cards. But how you guys explained it makes total sense. : )

*6 posts · started by Serraphael on 2025-01-03* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3433813)

**#2** · user `1719675` · 2025-01-04

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2025-01-04

[q="Weather Top"]I believe part of the set up is a reinforcement before the heroes take their turns.[/q]

---
**#4** · user `353779` · 2025-07-28

[q="Lord_Aethan"][q="Weather Top"]I believe part of the set up is a reinforcement before the heroes take their turns.[/q]
That is correct.[/q]
Hi, into a reinforcement phase (when you advance into the track) the mobs also move in this turn or the reinforcement phase only add new mob cards??

---
**#5** · user `1374367` · 2025-07-28 *(edited)*

[q="jaxsnop"]Hi, into a reinforcement phase (when you advance into the track) the mobs also move in this turn or the reinforcement phase only add new mob cards??[/q]
Step 1. Move Time Marker
Step 2. Roll Monster Die
Step 3. Monsters Move
Step 4. Monsters Attack
Step 5. Reinforcements

Reinforcements on turn A will not move until step 3 of the monster turn on turn B.

---
**#6** · user `353779` · 2025-07-29

OMG! How I din´t realize!!. TY

## Can Sweeping Strike only affect one additional monster or does the chain continue to the next clockwise monster?
*2 posts · started by Neriath on 2025-01-03* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3433445)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1394848` · 2025-01-03

The way I am reading Boldurs Sweeping Strike-card it only chains overkill damage to the next clockwise monster. But the artwork makes me a bit confused since it clearly shows Boldur hitting three enemies at the same time. 

Have I been understanding the card wrong? Does the chain continue?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2025-01-03

It is only 1 additional step. Here comes the problem of making artwork while the game still changes. He could previously cut through several monsters, but it was ultimately deemed too strong. Think of it as him using it in combination with Rapid Strike and it works again :)

## Dwarf Mail
*9 posts · started by wrobio on 2025-01-02* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3432879)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1512277` · 2025-01-02

As written, Dwarf Mail says "Prevent the first damage dealt to Boldur each monster turn". I have two questions:

1) Is this intended for the full monster turn, or each monster's attack? I assume the full turn, or it would be effectively doubling his inherent armor. 

2) It prevents a single damage, not all damage from one attack, right? As written, I could see it interpreted either way, but I assume it's meant to prevent a single damage each monster turn, since it doesn't have durability.

---
**#2** · user `1165219` · 2025-01-02

On the monsters turn, the first monster attack that causes damage to Boldur will be prevented, no matter the amount.  So make sure to take the biggest attack first so that one can be ignored.

If the first attack is 1 hit, which Boldur's armor would reduce to zero, that attack didn't cause damage thus the mail doesn't get used yet.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2025-01-02

That is unfortunately not the case, it is the first 1 damage that is prevented, not all damage from the first attack. However, you decide the order of effects, so you always let your armor block the first damage, and if there is more, the Dwarf Mail actually prevents the second damage. Effectively, this will prevent 1 damage per monster turn.

---
**#4** · user `1165219` · 2025-01-02

Oh!  I misread that then.  Luckily we haven't gotten to use it more than once so I haven't been abusing it *too* much :)

---
**#5** · user `4104618` · 2025-01-13

Oooh, we also thought it was all damage not just one. Good to know for future runs.

---
**#6** · user `1118358` · 2025-03-31 *(edited)*

The current wording on the card "Prevent the first damage dealt to Boldur each monster turn"*, could indeed be interpreted as allowing the player to choose which *first source* of damage to block. However, as the designer clarified, it was unfortunately meant to be written as “Prevent the first point of damage Boldur suffers each monster's turn" As it stands, the card has become a much less appealing.

*

---
**#7** · user `2756163` · 2025-03-31 *(edited)*

[q="Thiagoajorge"] The current wording on the card "Prevent the first damage dealt to Boldur each monster turn"*, could indeed be interpreted as allowing the player to choose which *first source* of damage to block. However, as the designer clarified, it was unfortunately meant to be written as “Prevent the first point of damage Boldur suffers each monster's turn" As it stands, the card has become a much less appealing.

*[/q]
Your well meant attempt at clarification again provides a very incorrect explanation that needs correcting. (This shows how English language requires very careful parsing)

The plural and especially the apostrophe you used in “each monster’s turn” again makes the chain mail too powerful since it would allow the chain mail to apply separately to each monster who attacks Boldur. 

“Prevent the first point of damage dealt to Boldur each monster turn"

## Questions on Initial Reinforcements + Monster Deck Events
*3 posts · started by LemonyFresh on 2025-01-01* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3432608)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `36112` · 2025-01-02

- The Threat "Raised" adds imps during reinforcement turns - does this activate during the initial Reinforcements?
- To make sure, events are still activated if drawn at the start of the game during initial Reinforcements, correct?

...and, a side Event question: "Unexpected Tricks" causes 1 Damage to be dealt to Boldur, which is prevented due to armor. If the next Monster card drawn is an event, does it Activate? Or was the dealt & blocked damage satisfactory in preventing the next event?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2025-01-02

Hi Anthony,

treat the initial setup of monsters as an ordinary reinforcement step, including events. Some events are not possible at this time, just skip them and draw the next card instead. If an event cannot be performed, it doesn't count as the 1 event / player. However, in the case you mention, where Boldur is dealt 1 damage, that happens even if he prevents it, and thus counts as 1 event.

---
**#3** · user `36112` · 2025-01-02

Thanks!

---

**#4** · user `1165219` · 2025-01-01

The skulls on the turn track are the turns that all the monsters charge.  Those last 4 turns are a rush!
You use both the yellow and red cards in both tracks.  Match the icon on each reinforce space with the back of the card (the shield behind the axes has either yellow paint or red paint, to match which card type to draw).  Legends should be mixed in as part of the normal deck.

Are you talking of the character's event cards?  Yes, you can play two at once.  Which are you trying to play?

## How many of each ability, and equipment can you have?
*3 posts · started by khenze on 2025-01-01* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3432440)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1879022` · 2025-01-01

Hey guys brand new to the game , having fun, now I’m pretty sure you can only have for event cards at one time , but what about abilities, and equipment?
Thanks

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2025-01-01

You can have any number of abilities and equipment. The only limitation is that you may only have 1 Main Weapon. If you ever get a new one, it replaces the old one (place it on top of the old one until the end of the game).

---
**#3** · user `1879022` · 2025-01-01

Thank you sir

## Event deck out of cards
*10 posts · started by coreside on 2025-01-01* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3432147)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1165219` · 2025-01-01

When you run out of your event cards, do you reshuffle the discard pile or can you no longer get more event cards?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2025-01-01

The events are shuffled into the monster card piles, so they shouldn't run out. But if they were to run out, you would simply reshuffle all used cards into a new pile to draw from.

Ah, no I meant your character deck.

Ah, sorry! Yes, just reshuffle the discarded cards into a new deck.

**#6** · user `2756163` · 2025-04-06

[q="LemonyFresh"]When your deck is empty?  Or when you need to draw and the deck is empty?  (Sindra's asking)[/q]
When you need to draw a card is standard for most games.
The lack of a draw deck only becomes a reality when one needs to draw a card. Until that point, one has Schrödinger's deck to draw cards from.

## Wrecking Balling Heroes Into and Out Of Grimheim
*4 posts · started by LemonyFresh on 2024-12-31* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3431404)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `36112` · 2024-12-31

It seems like it would useful to Wrecking Ball a friendly Hero into Grimheim!  This is legal, correct?!

And what exactly happens if you have Wrecking Ball, and you enter a Hero-filled Grimheim?!  May they be damaged and moved out?  May a subset be damaged and moved out, and some not?  MUST they be damaged and moved out?  😄

---
**#2** · user `4104618` · 2024-12-31

Great question! I would like to know this as well 😊

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-31

Yes, you may push another hero into Grimheim, giving them 1 damage. We worded this card with "character" rather than "monster" for this purpose. However, you cannot push someone out of there, as Grimheim is not an "occupied area" in that sense. Thematically, think of every character inside Grimheim to be inside one of the houses. Moving into Grimheim will not push anyone inside a building out of the building and also out into the surroundings. Not even Boldur has that force 😛 This way of reasoning will solve a lot of questions regarding Grimheim. If they are in Grimheim, they are inside one of the houses. That's why they are protected against attacks, that's why they cannot attack monsters outside, that's why they mend more effectively, etc.

---
**#4** · user `36112` · 2024-12-31

[q="Lord_Aethan"]Thematically, think of every character inside Grimheim to be inside one of the houses.[/q]I actually did utilize this!! I figured if anything could bust through a house wall, it might be a Wrecking Ball. :D

---

## How to understand ‘spend’ in quests
*10 posts · started by donmusse on 2024-12-30* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3431043)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `963073` · 2024-12-30

Hi all
Played the game once and had a blast 🙏
Some questions was raised throughout the game mainly upon the wording on how to complete quests.
The words spend was what left us confused.
(I have read the other threads - I hope - and spend and remove is the same, but use is different) 
 
The rulebook says, that if you spend an action to complete a quest, you don't get the other benefits of that action - easy enough.

Then a quest might say: spend 1 experience, spend 4 mana and so etc - but how is that to be understood: 

1) you spend four mana from one ability card and don't get to use that ability ? 
1a) you spend four mana to use an ability card and complete the quest as well?

2) how do you spend experience? 
Only thing from rulebook is when upgrading - is it then possible to use an action to spend experience or is it while you upgrade you complete the quest as well? 

Hope someone understands my questions and can help before playing again in a couple of hours 🙏

---
**#2** · user `1165219` · 2024-12-31

Quests that tell you to Spend Mana or Spend Gold (Experience) mean you must take the amount of Mana off of your cards or the Gold off of your board without being able to use it.   Sometimes it says Pay, sometimes Lose, and sometimes Remove, but they all mean the same thing and are just flavor.  Mana can come from several cards, it doesn't have to all come from one.

There is a quest that Sindra has to "Use 5 Mana in a single turn" and this means you actually do use the Mana to cast your skills.  She also has one to "Play 6 cards" which again lets you benefit from those cards.  But every quest that has you Spend something means you don't get the usual benefit from it.

---
**#3** · user `963073` · 2025-01-01

Thanks a lot for answering Luke 🙏

And to clarify:
To get 'home sewn tunic' I would then need to spend two separate actions to complete this quest.

One action to practice and one action to spend an experience (Gold).
- not getting any rewards from practice other than fulfilling the quest ?



[imageid=8620389]

---
**#4** · user `1165219` · 2025-01-01

Ah, for that one you spend just one action, a practice action.  Spending the experience isn't an action.  Be sure to place one of your two action markers on the practice action when you do this quest!

---
**#5** · user `963073` · 2025-01-02

Okay, so just one action (practice) but still remove1 experience token as well ?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#6** · user `430700` · 2025-01-02

Yes :)

---
**#7** · user `963073` · 2025-01-02

Great - I still only played once, but for future reference.
If the quest says spend or remove it should be understood like:
- if it's an action, you'll use that action (with no other reward than completing the quest )
- if it's mana, you can remove/spend mana from any combinations of cards
- if it's NOT an action, just a ressource (like experience/gold from the quest home sewn tunic) you'll just remove one ressource/experience at the same time as using the action.

Would the be correct ? 

And again - thanks a lot for your answers 🙏

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#8** · user `430700` · 2025-01-02

That's right, except an action isn't always involved at all. Some quests may say "Spend 2 gold in Grimheim". If so, it requires no action, it just requires you to be in Grimheim.

---
**#9** · user `303151` · 2025-06-17

Hi guys,
Can you clarify the "play 6 cards" requiriment?
Only the play events counts for this,distributed  in various turns??

Best regards!

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#10** · user `430700` · 2025-06-17

Yes, each time you play a card from your hand, add a crystal marker on the quest. When you have played 6 cards, you solve the quest and get the equipment.

## Monster Dice Charge Clarification  ✅
*10 posts · started by Yadayada23 on 2024-12-28* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3430060)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1430979` · 2024-12-29 *(edited)*

When you roll the monster dice and the result is [b]Charge[/b], do the rank 1 monsters charge immediately? And then move again during the Move step?

Rules say "roll the dice [b]and perform its effect[/b]", so that would suggest the charge happens and then they move again during the next step, "Monsters Move".

---
**#2** · user `36112` · 2024-12-29 *(edited)*

They do not move immediately.

How it works is, a Monster will have its Charge "toggle" either on or off, and the Charge affects only the Movement Step, providing a maxmium of one extra area of movement.

[b]A Monster will have its Charge "on" for a Movement Step if any of the below are true:[/b]
- the Monster is a Level 1 Monster (Goblin / Imp / Sprite), and the Charge face appeared on the die
- After its normal movement, the Monster is not in a position to attack a Hero, but would be if it moved one extra area [i]along its normal route to Grimheim[/i]
- the Time marker is on a Charge (skull) symbol on the Time track...thus enabling Charge for all Monsters on the board

[b]Remember:[/b]
- Whether Charging or not, a Monster will never leave an area during the Monster Movement Step if it is adjacent to a Hero (even mid-movement; it will stop if becomes adjacent to a Hero)
- During its Movement Step, a Monster will never alter its normal route to Grimheim
- It may be the case that [i]during its normal movement, a Monster will abandon an opportunity to attack[/i].  (This is relevant for Monsters with Ranged attacks - i.e. Fire Hordes).  This could then lead to a Charge, if advancing an additional area would then create a new opportunity to attack.   However...after its normal movement, a Monster will never then Charge [i]away[/i], if it landed in an area from which it could attack.
- a Charging Goblin (Level 1 Trollkin Monster) will move 3 areas, instead of its normal 2!!
- Not directly about Charging, but, remember that Legends are not blocked by other enemies...they will swap with them in order to move.

-----
[Edited based upon correction below - credit @pietu85]

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-29

Perfect summary, Anthony!

---
**#4** · user `1430979` · 2024-12-29

Thank you. The phrase "roll then perform its effect" tripped me up. Making it harder than it already is!

---
**#5** · user `95899` · 2024-12-30

[q="Lord_Aethan"]Perfect summary, Anthony![/q]

Anthony writes that a monster will charge if "A unit would be adjacent to a Hero if it Charged (not counting adjacency within Grimheim itself)"
But is that really the rule?

I though that a monster will charge if that allows it to [b]attack a hero[/b], not necessarily to move adjacent to a hero?

When considering the Fire Horde and their ranged attacks, there is a difference...

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#6** · user `430700` · 2024-12-30

Hi Jani, you are right, the rule is that they charge if that allows them to attack, so there is an important difference for the Fire Horde. "Perfect" was a bit exaggerated, but it was close :)

---
**#7** · user `36112` · 2024-12-30

Great catch!  It's been amended above.

---
**#8** · user `7872` · 2025-02-10 *(edited)*

Played for the first time this past weekend. We were confused on the charge mechanic. 
Just to be clear here…this charge does not give the extra movement to a monster unless it moves within attack range of a hero. 
If so…what is the point of them having a charge on the last few turns (on the turn track) if they always charge when they can attack. I guess I am confused here.
I thought maybe the turn track effect would let them move one extra space automatically even if they could not get within attack range.
I would love to be completely clear on how this works.
Thanks for any information people can provide here.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#9** · user `430994` · 2025-02-10

> ↳ *Replying to #8 (user `7872`):* Played for the first time this past weekend. We were confused on the charge mechanic. Just to be clear here…this charge does not give the extra movement to a monster unless it moves within attack range of a hero. If so…w…

> During those last turns, the monsters always charge (move their extra step), regardless of if they reach a hero. So they do indeed move an extra step, but don't move extra beyond that (this is instead of the normal charge rules), and they still stop on heroes.
>
> Cheers!

---
**#10** · user `36112` · 2025-02-10 *(edited)*

[q="diablo663"]Just to be clear here…this charge does not give the extra movement to a monster unless it moves within attack range of a hero.[/q]If it has Charge, it has the extra movement.

A Monster will have its Charge "on" (and thus giving extra movement) for a Movement Step if [i]any[/i] of the below are true:
- the time marker is on a Charge (skull) symbol on the time track
- the Monster is a Level 1 Monster (Goblin / Imp / Sprite), and the Charge face appeared on the die
- the Monster cannot currently attack a Hero following normal movement, but would be able to attack a Hero if it Charged

## Embla's starting equipment, Flimsy Blade
*4 posts · started by coreside on 2024-12-28* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3429475)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1165219` · 2024-12-28

Is her Flimsy Blade a "Main Weapon"?  I've been playing assuming it was (being a sword and all), but during my game just now I took a closer look and realized it doesn't say it is.  Does that mean it stacks with any new Main Weapon she gets?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-28

Her flimsy blade is not a main weapon. In a prototype, the effect on the sword read "May be considered a Main Weapon... with some imagination..." But we removed that for clarity and because you never actually want to count it as a main weapon. Once you get an _actual_ main weapon, it is a good backup blade in her left hand. Cheers!

When developing a game for this long, there are always plenty of additional content which couldn't fit the base game. I have shaved off many heroes, equipment, monsters and more, and some of it may very well return. I already have 6 more heroes in prototype form, and several smaller modules which could be simply added. Right now, what we need is the spreading of this game, to make the financial basis for an expansion warranted.

## Queen of the Hill: do you switch places if monster is killed?
*4 posts · started by Yadayada23 on 2024-12-27* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3429141)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1430979` · 2024-12-27 *(edited)*

Ability card reads: " deal two damage to an adjacent monster and switch places with it."

If that two damage kills the monster, do you still move to it's hex? I assume no.

And I assume you can't switch places with an enemy on a mountain space? But you still get to inflict the two damage?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

Queen of the Hill is a maneuver tactic, using your footwork offensively. So the movement is part of the effect and must be performed.
1) You still move, even if the monster is killed by the 2 damage. Thematically, it is the movement that deals the damage, because you are appearing behind them, giving them a gentle push down the hill.
2) You are right that you cannot move to a mountain area, and thus, you cannot use this tactic on monsters in a mountain area, unless you have the Fleetfoot ability on the upgraded side where you may move into mountain areas.

---
**#3** · user `1430979` · 2024-12-27

Thanks for the clarification. Glad I asked! 
I'm having fun with the game. The art and flavor text makes me laugh. 😆

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#4** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

Great to hear that! The humor is part of what sets it apart from other games :)

## Boldur: Dwarf mail and Wrecking ball
*6 posts · started by SpaceOgre on 2024-12-27* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3429134)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `4104618` · 2024-12-27

Played a really good game with Boldur just now and wanted to check that we did not overpower him 😉

Wrecking ball:
Is it possible to move into multiple occupied areas in the same move action?
When moving the character that was hit, does it need to be to an empty area?

Dwarf mail:
Since Boldur has normal armour we played that the Dwarf mail only triggered if Boldur receive more than 1 incoming damage during an attack.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

Wrecking Ball is amazing, but it requires you to use your move action. A lot of the time you want to move anyway, but not always. Once you have this ability, you'll likely not have any other actions left over than moving and attacking for the rest of the game.

Yes, the Wrecking Ball ability can be used for each step of your movement.

Dwarf Mail: It prevents to first damage, and you may choose which effect to apply in which order. So basically, you would always prevent with the Armor first, then if anything breaks through that, the Dwarf Mail prevents the first of those each turn.

---
**#3** · user `4104618` · 2024-12-28

Thank you for all the fast responses!

Just to clarify one more thing with Wrecking ball: does it work with Maneuver and Seek shelter? That is the way I would interper it since Wrecking ball only says move and not move action, but you mentioned move action above so wanted to make sure 🙂

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#4** · user `430700` · 2024-12-28

Yes, it is always active :)

---
**#5** · user `36112` · 2024-12-29 *(edited)*

Speaking of Seek Shelter:

- If the first space is used to enter a new (non-Grimheim) Location, must movement stop immediately, or can its 2nd movement still be used (but presumably while needing to stay in the same location)?

- Can it be used if already in a Location?
--- If so, can it be used to move out of a location, into a non-location area, and back into the same location, with its 2 movement?

This is all concerning not only Wrecking Ball, but also e.g. the Areas which come prepopulated with the various colors of gems.

Thanks!!

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#6** · user `430700` · 2024-12-29

1) The effect is to enter a location. You can select which area in that location you are targeting, which could be - for example - deeper inte the Troll Caves, thus moving 2 areas in the location.

2) Yes, it may be used if you are already in a location, and it may refer to the same location you are already in, even the same area, if you want to move out and then back in. Usually this will be unhelpful, since you cannot pause your movement in the middle to perform any action, but specifically collect the crystals, or advancing a quest which requires moving into X forests or so, this could be a good use of it.

## If an equipment quest says “spend 5 mana” or “remove 5 mana” if I spend 5 mana does this not count as remove? Bonus question “use 5 mana” cs the other 2 verbs?
*7 posts · started by RejectKid on 2024-12-26* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3428762)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `3613614` · 2024-12-26

Finkes has quests about spending and removing. I just don’t remember the cards.

---
**#2** · user `1165219` · 2024-12-27

Ah, I have this question too!  Just went to post but decided to read the new threads first.

The cards are Ring Of Au and Wizard's Hat.  One says to "Remove 7 Mana from your cards" and the other "Spend 4 Mana".  I'm curious if these are the exact same thing just stated with different words, or if there is a difference.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

"remove" and "spend" are the same, should have been "spend" for consistency. "Use" (found on Sindra's Trinket) means you need to use 5 mana while performing other effects to get it (typically teleporting with her ability and then using her Spark).

---
**#4** · user `3613614` · 2024-12-27

---
**#5** · user `3443597` · 2025-01-10

I also go the wizards hat a few turns later and did the same to get it. Was this correct?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#6** · user `430700` · 2025-01-10

No, when quests require you to spend or remove things, it is specifically a cost of the quest, you do not get the normal effecs. This applies to resources and actions spent. The only notable exception is one of Sindra's equipment where you need to "use 5 mana in one turn", then you may spend those resources on other things. That quest signifies that she uses a lot of power and accidentally forges a trinket.

## Movement clarification
*5 posts · started by Helkor on 2024-12-26* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3428710)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `533535` · 2024-12-26 *(edited)*

Using Ogre Valley Location as a example:

So if you have a brute in front of a Goblin where the Brute would move first and then the Goblin second. The Brute would move up one hex. The Goblin has a movement of 2. 

Would the goblin still stay behind the brute and just move one hex forward, and follow the hex path of the arrow in area of Ogre Valley? Or would it go around to the next empty hex toward Grimheim since it has one additional movement/charge?[imageid=8611400]

---
**#2** · user `533535` · 2024-12-26 *(edited)*

I found the answer by rereading page 8 in the rulebook if I understand it correctly. 

They move into the direction of the arrows until they either reach Grimheim or a road and I do not deviate from this path.  

So just for a little extra clarification if a goblin was left side of a brute with one hex between them on the brutes left side and the goblin has already moved its 2 movement.

Would the goblin break its forward path to Grimheim to charge one empty hex space to the right to take an attack action against the hero? Or would the goblin stay on it forward, movement to Grimheim?[imageid=8611429]

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

You need to be as simple-minded as the trollkin to grasp their suboptimal attack patterns 🙂
Monsters in this game only move forward (along their path to Grimheim), they never take detours or move sideways for any reason (except if the monster dice dictates that).
So in this case, the brute will move first and the goblin will only move 1 step before its path is blocked by the brute. This means, however, that even if the brute charges 1 extra step to attack, the goblin follows him to give support.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#4** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

Always forward 🙂 What they lack in brains, they make up for in numbers :)

---
**#5** · user `533535` · 2024-12-27

Thanks again for the clarification

---

Treetreader only gives 1 step into or out of a forest.

Any time, it is really useful and can sometimes mean you heal more efficiently with a move action in the forest than with the mend action.

## Does a move card/ability count as a move action? 
*2 posts · started by SpaceOgre on 2024-12-26* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3428644)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `4104618` · 2024-12-26

Played as Embla today and got the Ability that kills a rank 1/2 monster after a move action.

Can this be triggered by a card or ability that states "move X"? Or does it only work for move action?

We played it so it only worked on move action but wanted to check.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-26

Yes, it only works with a move action. Be mindful of the word "action" in other situations also, quite a lot of cards refer to your attack action, and they do not apply when using an event card or an equipment effect.

## More Fun with Finkel!  More Fun with Finkel!
*12 posts · started by LemonyFresh on 2024-12-26* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3428623)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `36112` · 2024-12-26 *(edited)*

I assume using "Deja Vu" on "Heat Death" doesn't do anything...."Play when you rolled any Runes against a non-Legend monster to Kill it"...i.e. it doesn't 'save' for your next roll or anything...

...so...some questions about what you CAN do with Deja Vu:

[imageid=8611194 large]

1) Deja Vu:  It states "once per turn"...does this also count the "Monster Turn," as it's own separate "turn", if the card you wish to play is reactive?

2) If so, and you play Blinding Flash, can you play it to stop attacks from 2 separate Monsters?  Or are you just sort of stopping the same monster's attack twice?

--- 2a) If you cannot stop 2 separate monsters' attacks, can you play it to stop the 2 Attacks from Grendel?

-----

Also...we finished a 5-0 victory run in our first go at the Campaign --- Alva & Finkel (Short Track).

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-26

Thanks for the questions! 🙂
Deja Vu is a strange ability, there is a reason we put it in the expansion and not in the core game! The monster turn is its own turn, so if you have a reaction card, you can use Deja Vu on it on the monster turn, but Blinding Flash doesn't work on 2 monsters, since - as you guessed - the effect is not "saved" until the next attack. However, it could work with Quick Reflexes to move extra steps. About Grendel, it is still 2 attacks, so it doesn't work there either, the effect doesn't linger until the second attack. Grendel's 2 attacks are separate, so players can cooperate to take 1 hit each, for example.

A 5-0 victory run with Alva and Finkel sounds too good to be true. Alva is pretty stable, but Finkel can't take more than just a couple of hits before he goes down, so I am curious how you pulled that off! Here is a quick checklist for things that I expect some players to get wrong:
1) Did you remember that goblins move 2 areas per turn instead of 1?
2) Did you remember that the Draugr has armor, so it always prevents 1 damage?
3) Did you play with the Monster Dice? (Because this is a quite significant difficulty increase, you need to have much larger margins when using the Monster Dice due to the uncertainty it adds).
4) Did you remember that mend actions may only heal your character, not equipment, unless you're in Grimheim?
5) Did you remember that all monsters charge if they can attack you (take 1 extra step)?

If you remembered all of these rules, then I am simply very impressed! Time for the longer track or the Monster Dice next! 🙂 Cheers!

The Threats in order were:

- Puny (Tier 3 & 4 enemies push)
- Fatigue (-1 heal on Mend)
- Far From Home (pull a monster card, start on any area shown, take 3 damage)

I'd say the long track campaign is next, but, I'm not sure.  I like the time length of the short track, and, I feel like you get to see "too much of your decks" with the long track, if you know what I mean.  I like that you chose to include both!

[size=9]---- incidentally, how does Far From Home work with Events in the deck?  We didn't pull one for that, our final game, but, just wondering.  Do you completely ignore the event and redraw? 🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#6** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

Wow, Fatigue is one of the most dangerous ones! It sounds like a very hard setup overall!
As for Far From Home, it doesn't perform the monster cards in any way, not placing any monster or perform any effect. Just draw until you have a card showing an area you can stand on.

🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#7** · user `430700` · 2024-12-27

Just one more thing, but it sounds like you have everything under control: you cannot attack or use suppressive fire from Grimheim. Suppressive Fire is one of the strongest cards in the game, but it doesn't actually kill any monster, and it "locks" your hero to a position near a flank you will most often not even want to finish off at all.

## Where do monster in Robber camp move to?
*2 posts · started by cattibrie_fr on 2024-12-26* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3428438)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `3174672` · 2024-12-26

Which direction monsters spawned in Robber Camp move to?

[imageid=8610834 medium]

I have assumed since this is Jotunn entering with other monsters from Spewing Mountain, Jotunn in Robber Camp would move to the road. But am I correct in that assumption? 

With my assumption a trollkin entering from Robber Camp with others from Ogre Valley would move to the right and not to the road.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-26

Imagine drawing lines from all the edge areas of the board (where there are arrows showing the direction). Once these lines enter a road area, they follow that road into Grimheim.
All monsters follow the "line" going through their area. So in this case, you have a line from the edge of the board, starting with the area with an Elemental, going straight to the robber camp. But the line continues until it reaches the road in front of the Robber Camp, so that's the path all monsters in the "line" will take.

So yes, the Jotunn in the Robber Camp will move into the road area, then follow the road.

---

## Fizzling Events
*4 posts · started by LemonyFresh on 2024-12-24* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3427853)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `36112` · 2024-12-25 *(edited)*

If a Monster-Deck Event would try to spawn enemies but it cannot because space is occupied, and then your next draw is also an Event, do you execute it (because the first event fizzled) or discard it (because you draw a maximum of one event per player per Reinforcement step)?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-25

The intention of the rule is to prevent too many events happening due to random shuffling. So in the vein of that intention, don't stop until you have actually performed 1 event. The ones that fizzle don't count (thematically, they never actually lead to an event)

---
**#3** · user `36112` · 2024-12-26

It sounds like you would say if there isn't a Trollkin on the board, it wouldn't count as "performed"?  Or does the "If" change things....

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#4** · user `430700` · 2024-12-26

That wouldn't count either, since nothing happened.

## Questions: Healing, Nailed together, Rune scroll
*2 posts · started by pietu85 on 2024-12-24* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3427513)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `95899` · 2024-12-24

Some questions:

1a.
Some cards, like the "Fountain of Youth", allows a [b]hero[/b] to [b]heal[/b].
Does that include the hero's equipment, or only the hero themselves?
In general, is [b]heal[/b] only for the hero, unless the effect specifically mentions otherwise?

1b.
I think the red crystals from the Troll Caves can be used to fix equipment, since rulebook mentions cardS, in prural... is that right?

2a.
Bjorn's "Nailed together" can deal damage to the [b]next monster behind[/b] the initial target.
I suppose this can reach farther than Bjorn's attack range?

2b.
"Nailed together" defines [b]behind[/b] as being [b]adjacent and further away[/b].
Does it mean that I can also choose an area that is diagonally further away than the target, not necessarily directly behind it?

3.
The promo pack equipment cards seem to mostly be especially effective ones, but Finkel'a [b]Rune Scroll[/b] appears... oddly weak?
I wonder if I somehow read it wrong?
Is it the same effect as with the other Scroll item, but with a steeper cost?
(I mean, spending 2 actions seems a lot costlier than just going to a certain location)

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-24

Hi Jani,

1a) "Heal" always refers to characters. An equipment card cannot be "healed".
1b) Yes! I am not sure this was the best idea we had, because it might cause confusion, but it makes it much more attractive!
2a) Yes, you only need to reach the first target.
2b) 2 areas are only adjacent if they share 1 side. There is no "diagonal" adjacency. So the second target must be exactly 1 step further away. This means, however, that Bjorn can curve-ball the arrow shot, hitting monsters in quite strange lines in optimal setups. It takes some extra imagination to visualize how he accomplishes this feat, but it's all part of the fun 🙂
3) Rune Scroll is the least inventive of the promo pack cards, as it is basically a copy of an already existing card. However, event cards are the bread and butter of wizards, and Finkel specifically, with his Deja Vu ability. He also has his Cane, which let's him easily save a move action every now and then, and can use that to effectively go into Grimheim and spend more valuable mend actions there before moving out again in the same turn with his move action. So he really excels with more cards and more equipment. And more mana, of course. Entering a certain location may take more than 2 actions, and may set you back even further. However, it could also take 1 move action if you happen to be close to it. But Highlands is one of the farthest away locations, so the probability of you being close to it is low.

---

## Sindra’s confusion ability
*7 posts · started by Sharaphin on 2024-12-24* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3427466)

🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-24

The troll attacks, not her. So it gets its trollkin support bonus, but not her extra dice. It is a bit ironic that a trollkin can get support by another troll when they are attacking each other, but Trolls are not smart enough to hold back...

## Finkel's Elemental Ring / Adjacency / Seer of Odin
*8 posts · started by LemonyFresh on 2024-12-23* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3427272)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `36112` · 2024-12-23 *(edited)*

Finkel's Elemental Ring: "Spend a mend action adjacent to [u]mountain, plains, and forest[/u]."

Does this all that have to be completed in one mend action, or can it be partially completed across turns?

---------

Also, incidentally, my assumption is that you are never considered "adjacent" to the space you are on - is that correct? [Edit: @Sharaphin pointed me to rules -- it doesn't quite say you are adjacent to the space you are standing on, but it says you are considered adjacent to its Terrain Type.  Unsure if there are other instances where adjacency to self matters.  Maybe casting a Level 2 Fireball -- it does 1 damage to all monsters adjacent to the attack target -- but I assume not to itself?]

---------

Also, also, rules on adjacency to Grimheim - from what I understand, the Heroes are not adjacent to anything except other Heroes in Grimheim, however Grimheim itself is adjacent to the surrounding spaces.  And when you "move out", you can move to a space adjacent to Grimheim...

...so, does this mean, for example, Finkel's Cane (move 1 Area) allows you to move out of Grimheim, however, Alva's Treetreader ([b]move into an adjacent Forest area, or move out of a Forest area[/b]) would allow entry into Grimheim from the forest, but [b]would NOT allow exit from Grimheim into the Forest?[/b]

It's a little counter-intuitive, however, I [i]believe[/i] that's how the rules read?  What is the intent?

(Unless...when you move, you are not moving to spaces "adjacent to your Hero", but to spaces "adjacent to your "area"?)

---------

Also, also, also -- Seer of Odin does one damage to all heroes everywhere --- is it true that those in Grimheim are still immune?

---------

Thanks!

---
**#2** · user `1789403` · 2024-12-23 *(edited)*

I think in the rules it says you are always adjacent to the spot you are in. 

On the back of the rules it says it.  Under clarifications.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-23

Hi Anthony, thanks for your questions!

1) The Element Ring is 1 mend action taken adjacent to all three terrain types at once.
2) You are considered to be adjacent to the terrain type you're in. For example, if you're standing in a plains area, with only forests and 1 mountain around you, you could claim the Element Ring with a mend action. If you are Embla with the ability to enter mountains, and you're standing on a mountain area surrounded by plains, you are still considered to be adjacent to mountain. Thematically, being adjacent to some terrain means having it at hands, and what would be more at hands than where you currently are?
3) You are correct, Treetreader may move into Grimheim but not out of it. Think of it this way: when you are inside Grimheim, you are inside one of its houses. You cannot jump out of the house onto the limbs of the trees of the forest. Viewing it this way usually solves most questions about Grimheim, including not being able to attack out from it, or being attacked from monsters outside, and why they do not stop their movement when adjacent to Grimheim when there are heroes inside, etc.
4) Seer of Odin reaches everyone, including heroes in Grimheim.

---

For example, I believe there is one that requires spending something like 4 Gold and a Practice action.  It sounds like maybe you must have to spend that all at once as well.  Is it, if the Quest requires different _types_ of things, they must all be performed at once?

2) Ok, great -- and so I take it that for other cases, you are not considered to be adjacent to the space you are in

3/4) Hmmm... I guess we can't keep that old dead skeleton lady from seeing into our houses!!! :D

Thanks Jonathan!!  Great game!!

If I cast Fireball II and make Damage to adjacent Enemies is this damage increased too or only the damage to the first target? And can I use lightning rod to spend mana and increase the damage to an adjacent enemy.
Greetings Mike

🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#6** · user `430700` · 2025-01-19

The emphasis is on the monster. Each time a monster is dealt damage, spend 1 mana to deal 1 more. In the optimal Fireball II effect, you attack 1 monster and deal 1 damage to 6 adjacent monsters. If you want to deal an extra damage to all of them, you need to spend 7 mana.

## Maneuver
*6 posts · started by HORST324 on 2024-12-23* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3427182)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `113253` · 2024-12-23

First of all, great looking game! Just got my pledge yesterday (the whole kaboodle) and the production is fantastic. Very well done! 
Reading the rules now and I understand all pretty well. One question regarding the Monster die ... How exactly is the "Maneuver" result enacted? I assume it means that the monster moves past the hero to the next space behind the hero (as long as that space is a legal space to enter). Does the clockwise/counterclockwise description mean anything? Do you physically move the monster around the adjacent spaces of that hero in the given direction? And if so, is it then blocked from doing so if those spaces are occupied or otherwise impassable? 
Thanks!
Herm

---
**#2** · user `36112` · 2024-12-23 *(edited)*

Imagine centering the die right atop the hero.  All adjacent monsters physically move [u]one[/u] space in the direction of the arrow, around the hero, [b]simultaneously[/b].

If anything is in the way (a hero, or the edge of the board), then some monsters may indeed be blocked from moving.  But monsters in general wouldn't block each other, as they are moving all at once.

If the Hero is adjacent to the home base, then that may lead to a monster entering, and a structure being destroyed.

Remember to trigger the effect for every Hero, and in turn order.  Chain effects can occur if heroes are near each other.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-23

Hi Hermann, glad to see more US backers getting the game! 
There are six areas around each hero, so moving clockwise around the heroes means moving from one adjacent area to the next adjacent area to the right.
Imagine an analog clock with the hero in the center, monsters move like the clock dialys. This happens simultaneously, so if there are 6 monsters surrounding the hero, they can all move. They may still be blocked from moving of other heros are in their way, but they may "rotate" into Grimheim.

---
**#4** · user `36112` · 2024-12-23

Got ya by 11 seconds!  😝

---
**#5** · user `113253` · 2024-12-23

Thank you both for the quick answers! OK ... got it. I just wasn't sure if the clockwise/counterclockwise movement reference was to be taken literally ... actually physically moving the monsters around the hero ... or if it was more narrative ... just describing how the monsters end up in the area behind the hero. Sounds good and will be starting play later today. Thanks!

---
**#6** · user `1127492` · 2025-03-15

Ok. The key is „move [u]one[/u] space“

This is not described in the rules, but now this makes sense

## Rule & strategy questions
*4 posts · started by grundarn on 2024-12-23* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3427095)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `2664812` · 2024-12-23

Hi, and thank you for a great game added to the co-op collection (assuming Fryxelius will answer as they've done a splendid job so far). Since delivery we've put down Spirit Island and done 10+ plays of Fate, a few on the longer monster axis (although no successful runs!).

Coming from a group who absolutely adores Terraforming Mars, we really like the game as a semi-simple, easy-to-introduce, co-op game, but I love being a stickler for rules and some fringe rulings have come up!

-Embla's Queen of the Hill. 
   1, are you required to change place? 
   2, do you still change places if the monster dies?

-Alva's Singing Bow. It's unlocked when you've rolled 10 damage dies in a forest, does that mean you gain the effect of it on the same attack as you unlock it?

Thank you, and merry christmas!

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-23

Thanks Victor! I believe we use some similar techniques to make the games replayable, with quite clear rule sets and multitudes of combinations through card interactions.

Embla's Queen of the Hill:
1) Yes, you must switch places with it. Thus, she cannot use this with a monster in a mountain area, because she cannot move into it.
2) Yes, you still switch places with it, even if it dies.

Thematically, her ability is about using footwork to gain the upper hand, using movement as an offensive tactic.

Alva's Singing Bow is indeed unlocked when you have rolled 10 attack dice in a forest. However, it says that whenever you roll the runes, you add extra dice, but they were already rolled to unlock the card, so it doesn't apply. However, if you roll your attack dice and unlock the card, then play the card Mastery which adds 4 more dice in the same attack, those might trigger the effect of her new bow.

Cheers!

---
**#3** · user `2664812` · 2024-12-23

Thank you for the quick reply! However, I think you got Alva's bows confused :) Singing bow gives a mana after each attack. I interpret your answer as yes, you do get the mana bonus on the attack you unlock it with.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#4** · user `430700` · 2024-12-23

Haha, how embarrassing! I blame it on seeing these bows with many different names through development 🙂 Yes, you would get the mana immediately.

## Questions about Monster Charge and Hero Adjacency, as Well as Legendary Monster Type Bonuses
*7 posts · started by bktanner on 2024-12-22* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3426902)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `313081` · 2024-12-23

Played my first game tonight, 2 players, had a lot of fun, got brutally crushed.

Had 2 rules questions that came up:

If a monster is charging (during the last 4 rounds of the game for example), will it stop if it moves adjacent to a hero after the first movement? We had a situation where we were attempting to body block monsters from reaching Grimheim and the situation worked out such that the 1st move put them adjacent to a hero, but the 2nd move would run them into the city (thus causing us to lose the game). From the rules it sounds like they will only not move if they START the movement phase adjacent to a hero, but will charge past a hero once their move has started - is this correct?

Second question: We drew a red card which spawned the legendary monster Nidhuggr and a couple of fire elementals on the "legends" quadrant of the map (not the Fire Horde quadrant) - do the elementals still count as "fire horde" monsters for the purposes of the 2 attack range bonus that all Fire Horde monsters have? What about Nidhuggr? It was unclear to me since they spawned in the "legends" map quadrant where there is no bonus listed on the board. Do other legendary monsters get the monster type bonuses if they spawn in that monster's location (e.g. if they spawn in the dark forest / trollkin quadrant do they get the attack bonus)? What about if they spawn in the "legend" quadrant, how would I tell what monster type bonus they are supposed to get?

Thanks!

---
**#2** · user `36112` · 2024-12-23

[q="bktanner"]If a monster is charging (during the last 4 rounds of the game for example), will it stop if it moves adjacent to a hero after the first movement? We had a situation where we were attempting to body block monsters from reaching Grimheim and the situation worked out such that the 1st move put them adjacent to a hero, but the 2nd move would run them into the city (thus causing us to lose the game). From the rules it sounds like they will only not move if they START the movement phase adjacent to a hero, but will charge past a hero once their move has started - is this correct?[/q]I was wondering the same.  I figured that most likely, they stop in the middle of movement if they move adjacent to a Hero, though I cannot justify it from the rules.

---
**#3** · user `36112` · 2024-12-23

(they do stop)

---
**#4** · user `36112` · 2024-12-23

---
**#5** · user `313081` · 2024-12-23

[q="LemonyFresh"]Looks like it was answered:  https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3423565/article/45343799#45343799

(they do stop)[/q]

Bah! I even scanned the rules posts before asking (there aren’t many) and some how missed that very obvious thread!

---
**#6** · user `36112` · 2024-12-23

😄

To be fair, that specific Legend is the ONE Legend whose type doesn't correspond to any of the three main enemy types (Type "Wyrm").

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#7** · user `430700` · 2024-12-23

Great to see a community helping each other! It seems you already got your answer, but here it is again:
1) Monsters adjacent to heroes don't move, regardless of when they become adjacent. So if they become adjacent in the middle of a move, they stop. If they are already adjacent, they don't move. The only exception to this is when you roll the monster dice and it tells monsters to move around the heroes. But this is not in the move phase, so their normal move rules don't apply there.

2) Legends have no "quadrant of the map", they only have a tile supply in one corner of the game board. Each faction (trollkin, fire horde, and undead) have 2 spawn zones each (trollkin come from Ogre Valley and Dark Forest, fire horde from Spewing Mountain and Highlands, and undead from Marsh of Sorrow and Dead Plains). The faction effects apply to monsters of that faction, regardless of where they show up. For instance, if you roll the Ambush side of the monster dice, goblins will appear adjacent to heroes, regardless of where that is. This doesn't turn them into undead of fire horde, they are still trollkin. Legends have a faction written on the legend card. Since Nidhuggr specifically is a Wyrm and not a Fire Horde, it doesn't have attack range +1.

---

## Questions! (RuneStone start, claiming gems from board, building town pieces)
*5 posts · started by LemonyFresh on 2024-12-22* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3426710)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `36112` · 2024-12-22

1) Does the RuneStone start the game on, or off the board?  If on the board, what is the use of the initial charge symbol?

2) When you claim gems from the board, must you take all of them?

3) Can you "build" (with an event) more Town pieces than the game initially started with?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-22

1) on the first step. The initial symbol is not for charge, but for reinforcements. It is a reminder to start the game with the first wave of monsters already in play.

2) You may take any number of them.

3) Yes, but not more than there are actual pieces.

---
**#3** · user `36112` · 2024-12-22 *(edited)*

[q="Lord_Aethan"]1) on the first step. The initial symbol is not for charge, but for reinforcements. It is a reminder to start the game with the first wave of monsters already in play.[/q]Wait - were the skulls and reinforcement icons / instructions mixed up in the rules?
[imageid=8605897 medium]
[imageid=8605915 medium]

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#4** · user `430700` · 2024-12-22

No, this looks right. But the time marker doesn't start at the corner of the game board. The game ends with 4 charge turns, the big climax where all monsters rush for 4 turns to get into the village. It starts at the other end.

## Bjorn and Embla's hero abilities
*9 posts · started by coreside on 2024-12-22* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3426704)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `1165219` · 2024-12-22

Just got my copy, played one 2-player game.  Really fun so far, but we had a few initial questions.

Is Embla's ability that she moves 4 instead of 3 on a move action?  Or is that a "Move 4" free action that she can take every turn?  We played it the first way, but after the game I scoured through the rulebook and it leads me to believe we did it wrong, and she can activate her hero card as a free action to Move 4.

I was struggling with Bjorn's hero ability.  It says to "spend 1 focus action", so I took that to work like quests do, where I have to actually place an action token on the focus action to get the 2 damage but I don't get the usual focus action benefit.  If so, this feels really limiting and underpowered compared to the other heroes.  Granted I don't know the balance of anything yet given my one play.  But the other heroes all have some passive bonus that applies practically every turn at no cost, and Bjorn's reads more like "spend one of your two actions to deal 2 damage, but only to the thing you just hit" and makes him feel incredibly action limited.  Now, guaranteed damage can be useful in certain situations, but it just felt like it didn't measure up to the other actions which would end up giving much better tactical or strategic advantage.

Loving the game though!

---
**#2** · user `1789403` · 2024-12-22

He has an ability that lets him send overkill damage into a monster behind the current target. If you hit hard enough you can kill two things. This spend of an action could be enough to do the double kill.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-22

Thanks for your questions!
Embla has move 4 instead of move 3. Now that you mention it, I understand why this might be confusing. Strange that this never became a question through all our betatesters...

You are correct about Bjorn's effect, it requires you to actually place an action marker on the focus action space. Bjorn is the hero that has the best potential to take down Bosses in a single shot. He has several ways to get additional range, so his best option is to find a spot where he can stand still and use both actions for attacking. Dealing 2 damage is not a wasted action, it is generally more than event cards deal. If you upgrade Bjorn, it becomes 3 instead of 2.

---
**#4** · user `1165219` · 2024-12-22

Ah!  I hadn't seen that ability yet (still haven't looked through all the cards), that definitely makes it better.
Thanks for your answers both of you!  Can't wait to get back in for more play sessions.  This feels like it will become one of my game night staples.

## Smitebiter card for Boldur
*4 posts · started by Helkor on 2024-12-22* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3426678)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `533535` · 2024-12-22 *(edited)*

Smitebiter card for Boldur states: This is your Main Weapon. If you kill a monster in an attack action, any excess damage may be stored here (max 3 stored). Damage stored here may be added to your attack action.

I'm assuming that you remove the damage when you use it on your next attack? Or does it stay on the weapon card for the rest of the game?

Also does all the damage that is stored gets used on the next attack or can you use what is needed to slay the enemies?

---
**#2** · user `1789403` · 2024-12-22

It says may be used. So I played it where if I needed it after the dice were rolled, I would spend the damage.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-22

You may use (and thus remove the markers) any number of them. This may be chosen after the dice roll. So this makes it more interesting in which order you attack your enemies. Start by attacking someone weak in the plains, storing up some excess damage. Then attack someone unwounded in a forest, where you can add these damages regardless of their cover.

---
**#4** · user `533535` · 2024-12-23

Thanks for the replies and clarification.

## Finkel’s Power Staff?
*4 posts · started by jonnel on 2024-12-22* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3426581)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `233443` · 2024-12-22

To get Finkel’s Power Staff, you must ”Deal 3 damage to yourself in the Temple Ruins”.

Do you need to succesfully attack (yourself) and have at least 3 hits on the dices, or can you just assume that you auto-succeed in maiming yourself and just take 3 damages?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-22

As Yoda said: "Do or do not, there is no try". This quest signifies the dangers Finkel has to go through to get hold of the staff, so the damage is dealt to him by the place. Cheers!

---
**#3** · user `2973645` · 2025-11-14

Do you have to end your movement for this quest, then do the damage to yourself?
Or, if you are adjacent to the Temple Ruins, can you move one space to enter, deal three damage, then use your remaining two movement?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#4** · user `430700` · 2025-11-14

No, solving a quest is not an action, unless it says so. You cannot perform actions while moving, but some Quests even requires you to do them within other actions.

## When upgrading abilities or characters? Also question about Troll Caves location.
*3 posts · started by Helkor on 2024-12-21* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3426357)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `533535` · 2024-12-22 *(edited)*

When upgrading abilities or characters?

1) Do you keep the damage done to heroes when you upgrade their character card or does it clear the damage on the character card whenever upgraded?

2) Do you clear heroes abilities damage or mana from abilities cards whenever they are upgraded?

3) On Troll Caves, what spots are open for the heroes to move into?  Because it stated that the troll caves have mountains on three sides.  So I wasn't sure on the legal movement for the heroes.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-22

Hi Helkor,

for 1) and 2), the answer is that all markers on these cards stay even when the cards upgrade.

for 3), the Troll cave is 3 areas, and each of those areas are mountain areas, with the rule exception that players may move there (thematically because of the cave). So you can treat all these 3 areas as mountain areas, but you may still move there as a hero.

---
**#3** · user `533535` · 2024-12-22

OK, thanks for the clarification.  I figured that's how it would be, but I just didn't know for sure. I thought I might've read it in the book, but I just couldn't find it.

## More questions...
*6 posts · started by Robert Olesen on 2024-12-20* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3425406)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `218275` · 2024-12-20 *(edited)*

I played twice yesterday with two other playes, and that generated some questions.

This game creates enthusiasm and frustration, which sometimes inspires creative interpretations of the rules and card texts or questions about the exact meaning of those texts. A FAQ would IMO be helpful, but at least we have this forum.

1) Location bonuses: Do you need to end movement in the area with the bonus to get those bonuses (3 mend, 3 gold, 3 mana) or can you pick them up while passing through? The rules state "a hero there may ..." which does not answer that question in my mind.

2) A player had Alvas Windbite bow with the text "Whenever you roll runes, add another die to your roll for each rune". She wanted to apply that to all dice rolled by Alva as the formulation is general, but we argued that it can only be applied in the context of an attack action (where the bow is applied). Which is correct?

3) A player used Finkels Deja Vu II ability to prevent two monster attacks with Blinding Flash, and then return Blinding Flash to his hand. Can Blinding Flash be used with Deja Vu? Deja Vu states that you can use it "Once per turn", which could be interpreted to be a player turn (not including monster attacks) or once per player and monster turn.

4) Embla has an ability that lets her swap place with a monster. I assume that she cannot swap place with a monster in a mountain area. Correct?

5) We somehow got confused about mountains, and got the impression that heroes cannot attack monsters in mountains. Part of the confusion was connected to Boldurs Orebiter, which seemed to let him attack monsters in mountains and get gold for each hit. After some discussion and rules checks, we finally decided that heroes CAN attack (but not move) into mountains and Boldurs Orebiter is designed to let him "attack" into an empty adjacent mountain hext in order to mine some gold. Correct?

---
**#2** · user `36112` · 2024-12-20

Sorry - I don't have the answers, but wondering -- any quick review you can give?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-12-20 *(edited)*

Quick answer written on my phone: 
1) You do not have to stop, you can simply pass through and gather the bonus resources. However, note that the resources are placed on a specific area inside the location, they cannot be connected from any of the areas in the location. 

2) The Windbite effect applies all the time. We have tried to be specific when something only applies in attack actions. 

[-]3) The monster turn is also a turn. The issue in this case is that each attack is separate and not simultaneous (in the order chosen by the players). For example, if Embla can kill a trollkin in a defense situation, that may alter the trollkin support in a subsequent attack against her. So the monster attacks happen one at a time. Therefore, using Deja Vu on Blinding Flash doesn't help, because you can only prevent one attack anyway - the current one.[/-]
EDIT: I am sorry, the card was only meant to be used on your own turn, but since it didn't clarify it, I explored how it could work if we lifted that requirement. However, it creates some crazy combos which are not good for the game. So Deja Vu may only be used on YOUR turn.

4) Correct!

5) Yes, heroes can attack monsters in mountains. Boldur's Orebiter lets him attack the mountain itself (occupied or not) to gain gold instead of dealing damage.

I hope you are having a great time!

---

Therefore, using Deja Vu on Blinding Flash doesn't help, because you can only prevent one attack anyway - the current one.

## Circle of Life ✅
*2 posts · started by Robert Olesen on 2024-12-17* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3423994)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `218275` · 2024-12-17

Sindras starting equipment (Circle of Life) can store damage taken by Sindra. It states that each time Sindra takes a mend action, the Circle of Life is repaired for 1 damage. It does not say if this is additional to the other damage removed by the mend action, or if it is part of the damage she can mend (usually 2 or 5 in total).

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430994` · 2024-12-17

> ↳ *Replying to #1 (user `218275`):* Sindras starting equipment (Circle of Life) can store damage taken by Sindra. It states that each time Sindra takes a mend action, the Circle of Life is repaired for 1 damage. It does not say if this is additional to the…

> Circle of Life repairs itself by 1 each time you take a Mend action, regardless what you do with that mend action. So it is in addition to the normal effect.
>
> Cheers!

## Sindra / Mana questions
*2 posts · started by Robert Olesen on 2024-12-17* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3423987)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `218275` · 2024-12-17 *(edited)*

Sindras hero card allows her to spend 3 mana and a move action to move anywhere on the map. That hero card does not generate mana, and it doesn't say where the 3 mana are supposed to come from. She also has a card that moves mana around, so....
1) Does the mana need to come from the hero card when spent, or
2) Can it be taken from any card with mana?

She also has an ability that can generate mana to ANY card. Can this put mana on cards that do not generate mana (e.g. her hero card)?

This is a great game. Fun, challenging and with lots of toys on the cards to play with 😀

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-17

Hi Robert,
As a rule, only cards that generate mana can store it, and as a follow up rule, cards use mana on themselves when using their effects, unless otherwise stated. However, if a card that doesn't generate mana uses it, it can take such mana from any card in that players tableau. So Sindra may use mana from any of her cards, and even from several cards at once, to pay for her hero ability.

---

## Monsters Move in Charge
*2 posts · started by Leevertti on 2024-12-16* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3423565)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `4092647` · 2024-12-16

The rules say: "Monsters adjacent to heroes NEVER move in this phase." 

What should you do if a monster moves next to a hero and still has the chance to move one area forward according to the charge (end game situation)? Does moving next to a hero stop the monster's movement or is that a continuous move that still moves the monster one area forward according to the charge? In both cases, the monster stays next to the hero, but in the second case it moves one area further.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-16

As soon as it is adjacent to a hero, it stops, regardless of how many movements it may take. So it may stop mid-movement. Cheers!

## Attack into Grimheim allowed? ✅
*7 posts · started by Robert Olesen on 2024-12-15* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3422700)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `218275` · 2024-12-15

I can't find it in the (otherwise quite explicit) rulebook, so I wonder:
Can monsters attack a hero in Grimheim? Would they charge to get adjacent to Grimheim in order to attack a hero there?

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#2** · user `430700` · 2024-12-15

No, heroes in Grimheim cannot interact with characters outside and vice versa.

> [q="helgerg"]Then I assume that a hero inside grimheim won't stop a monster from moving into grimheim, as they are not considered adjacent? [/q]
> Correct.
> One of the hardest parts of the late game is making sure you have space to stand outside Grimheim to stop all those monsters from entering (without being knocked out yourself of course):
>
> Cheers!

**#6** · user `36112` · 2024-12-22

[q="Lord_Aethan"]No, heroes in Grimheim cannot interact with characters outside and vice versa.[/q]

🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#7** · user `430700` · 2024-12-22 *(edited)*

Depends. Usually, maneuvering takes you outside of Grimheim, which allows you to interact with monsters outside. But you cannot play "Kick", for example. Thematically, imagine you are inside a house. I think most rules will make sense that way.

## Belt of youth Item - how to track the quest?
*3 posts · started by yetiboy on 2024-08-19* — [link](https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/3353486)

📌 OP<br>**#1** · user `337862` · 2024-08-20

How does the card work? What I mean is how do you keep track of entering 8 forests?  Can the player move into and out of the same  forest space and would that count? I'm assuming that the player doesn't  have to visit all 8 on the same turn.

---
**#2** · user `1048591` · 2024-08-20

[q="yetiboy"]How does the card work? What I mean is how do you keep track of entering 8 forests?  Can the player move into and out of the same  forest space and would that count? I'm assuming that the player doesn't  have to visit all 8 on the same turn.[/q]
You can visit the same, but more efficient to walk between forest spaces. You add a marker to your card each forest you enter until you reach 8. You can't usually do it in one turn, as you won't have that many steps to walk.

---
🎲 **DESIGNER — confirmed**<br>**#3** · user `430700` · 2024-08-20

Örjan is right. You need to enter 8 forests, any forests, and you may enter the same several times. Keep track with crystal markers or damage dice.
This quest is not always easy to accomplish, but Alva has several effects that help her movement, including her ability Treetreader, which will be effective for this.

---
